# We are located 20 minutes west of  Charlottesville, Virginia in gorgeous Nelson County.

# 151 Veritas Lane  Afton, Virginia 22920

We are a proud member of the Nelson 151 Trail. For more information, please visit:

[www.nelson151.com](https://www.nelson151.com/)

For several years in my winter newsletter, I used to bemoan the fact that there was no real winter, but this year made up for all those non-winters combined.

### March 16, 2026

## [A Remarkable Virginia Winter: Snow, New Wines & Vineyard Life](https://veritaswines.com/a-remarkable-virginia-winter-snow-new-wines-vineyard-life/)

[![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/Winter-scaled.jpeg)](https://veritaswines.com/a-remarkable-virginia-winter-snow-new-wines-vineyard-life/ "A Remarkable Virginia Winter: Snow, New Wines & Vineyard Life")

[Read More](https://veritaswines.com/veritas-in-the-fall-harvest-to-holidays-at-the-vineyard/ "Veritas in the Fall: Harvest to Holidays at the Vineyard")

There really is something magical about the sudden transformation from pedestrian green to canary yellow from verdure to alizarin crimson and firetruck red. It is not just the change that is a miracle in and of itself, but the incredible contrasts in colors amplified by the close bosomed friend of the maturing sun.

### November 25, 2025

## [Veritas in the Fall: Harvest to Holidays at the Vineyard](https://veritaswines.com/veritas-in-the-fall-harvest-to-holidays-at-the-vineyard/)

[![dirt road with fall foliage](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/1-Autumn-Colors-scaled.jpeg)](https://veritaswines.com/veritas-in-the-fall-harvest-to-holidays-at-the-vineyard/ "Veritas in the Fall: Harvest to Holidays at the Vineyard")

[Read More](https://veritaswines.com/summer-at-veritas-ripening-vines-and-remarkable-moments/ "Summer at Veritas: Ripening Vines and  Remarkable Moments")

Summer time, it’s hot and humid, it is the hottest and the most humid month of the year. It’s as if we are dogged by the “Dog Star” Sirius which is the brightest star in the heavens from late July to early August, the so-called “dog days of summer.” Dogged because it is that very \[…\]

[Read More](https://veritaswines.com/a-look-back-at-winter-2025-at-veritas/ "Frozen Vines and Gold Medal Wines: A Look Back at Winter 2025 at Veritas")

Frozen Vines and Gold Medal Wines: A Look Back at Winter 2025 at Veritas. It is hard to understand how this winter could have been so darn cold. We’ve been in Virginia for 25 years, and this was undoubtedly the longest prolonged spell of cold weather. I have been bemoaning that in the last few winter newsletters or so, we haven’t had a decently cold winter, but this one has made up for it in spades (or shovels of snow).

It is not just the change that is a miracle in and of itself, but the incredible contrasts in colors amplified by the close bosomed friend of the maturing sun.

We’ve been in Virginia for 25 years, and this was undoubtedly the longest prolonged spell of cold weather. I have been bemoaning that in the last few winter newsletters or so, we haven’t had a decently cold winter, but this one has made up for it in spades (or shovels of snow).

[Read More](https://veritaswines.com/veritas-in-the-fall-harvest-to-holidays-at-the-vineyard/ "Veritas in the Fall: Harvest to Holidays at the Vineyard")

There really is something magical about the sudden transformation from pedestrian green to canary yellow from verdure to alizarin crimson and firetruck red. It is not just the change that is a miracle in and of itself, but the incredible contrasts in colors amplified by the close bosomed friend of the maturing sun.

### November 25, 2025

## [Veritas in the Fall: Harvest to Holidays at the Vineyard](https://veritaswines.com/veritas-in-the-fall-harvest-to-holidays-at-the-vineyard/)

[![dirt road with fall foliage](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/1-Autumn-Colors-scaled.jpeg)](https://veritaswines.com/veritas-in-the-fall-harvest-to-holidays-at-the-vineyard/ "Veritas in the Fall: Harvest to Holidays at the Vineyard")

[Read More](https://veritaswines.com/a-look-back-at-winter-2025-at-veritas/ "Frozen Vines and Gold Medal Wines: A Look Back at Winter 2025 at Veritas")

Frozen Vines and Gold Medal Wines: A Look Back at Winter 2025 at Veritas. It is hard to understand how this winter could have been so darn cold. We’ve been in Virginia for 25 years, and this was undoubtedly the longest prolonged spell of cold weather. I have been bemoaning that in the last few winter newsletters or so, we haven’t had a decently cold winter, but this one has made up for it in spades (or shovels of snow).

### March 14, 2025

## [Frozen Vines and Gold Medal Wines: A Look Back at Winter 2025 at Veritas](https://veritaswines.com/a-look-back-at-winter-2025-at-veritas/)

[![A Look Back at Winter 2025 at Veritas](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/03/1-Winter-edited.png)](https://veritaswines.com/a-look-back-at-winter-2025-at-veritas/ "Frozen Vines and Gold Medal Wines: A Look Back at Winter 2025 at Veritas")

Spring 2026

Spring 2026

- **Four-Day Farmhouse Retreats**\- Once a month in April, May _(retreat is full_), and June
- **[Supper Series Begins](https://veritaswines.com/supper-series) \-** Friday, May 29
- **Monticello Wine Week -**(Dates to be Announced)

Summer 2026

Summer 2026

- **Supper Series Continues -** Friday, June 26, Friday, July 24, and Friday, August 21
- **Starry Nights**\- Saturday, August 22
- **Four-Day Farmhouse Retreats -** Once a month in July and September

Fall 2026

Fall 2026

- **Last Supper Series -** Friday, September 25
- **Four-Day Farmhouse Retreats -** Starting October 4, Oct. 11, Oct. 18, Oct. 25, November 1, and Nov. 8
- **Veritas Illuminated Begins -** Friday, November 27

Winter 2026

Winter 2026

- **New Year's Eve Masked Ball -** Thursday, December 31, 2026

# These all-inclusive retreats are a wine lover's dream amidst the breathtaking 120 acres of Veritas Vineyard and Winery. Guests can indulge in yoga, Blue Ridge Mountain hikes, farm-to-table meals, exclusive winery tours, and plenty of exceptional wine—all designed to help you recharge, no matter the reason. These all-inclusive extended escapes include time to relax with a good book, enjoy a massage, or simply enjoy a moment for yourself. Pricing starts at $2,500 per room (double occupancy) and includes fine dining breakfast, lunch and dinner options, wine, yoga, hiking, cooking classes, and more.

[****FARMHOUSE FOUR-DAY RETREAT****](https://www.veritasfarmhouse.com/four-day-retreat)

# SUNDAY THROUGH WEDNESDAY

# APRIL 12TH - 15TH

[**ONE ROOM REMAINING**](https://www.veritasfarmhouse.com/four-day-retreat)

[**INQUIRE NOW**](mailto:farmhouse@veritasfarmhouse.com)

[**MEMBER  REGISTRATION**](https://www.exploretock.com/veritaswines/event/589101/wine-line-with-andrew-hodson)

# Join Owner Andrew Hodson for an engaging, educational tasting of Veritas' sparkling wine lineup. Learn about our sparkling program, how we use the traditional method (the same technique used in Champagne), and enjoy an afternoon full of fine bubbles, small bites, and a class well worth attending... it is all about wine, of course. Club Members are invited to attend these sessions free of charge as part of their membership, including bringing one guest.     Members of the general public may join the waitlist and attend for $25 per person if space allows. Email wineclub@veritaswines.com to be added to the waitlist.     Sign up today, and learn more about joining the Veritas Wine Club to enjoy this and other exclusive benefits.

# Join Owner Andrew Hodson for an engaging, educational tasting of Veritas' sparkling wine lineup. Learn about our sparkling program, how we use the traditional method (the same technique used in Champagne), and enjoy an afternoon full of fine bubbles, small bites, and a class well worth attending... it is all about wine, of course. Club Members are invited to attend these sessions free of charge as part of their membership, including bringing one guest.     Members of the general public may join the waitlist and attend for $25 per person if space allows. Email wineclub@veritaswines.com to be added to the waitlist.    Sign up today, and learn more about joining the Veritas Wine Club to enjoy this and other exclusive benefits.

# MAY 28TH

# THURSDAY

[**JOIN OUR WINE CLUB**](https://veritaswines.com/wine-club)

# Save the date, our fourth annual Supper Series kicks off this May! Our family-style Supper Series will spotlight seasonal and regional foods in a chef-driven dining experience. Our talented Culinary Team is dedicated to providing you with an outstanding Supper, ensuring your wish to return for each unique dinner. For our May dinner, French flavors, Veritas wines, and a cozy evening at the vineyard await.

# **Price:** $100, including wine pairings and service, taxes and fees not included.  _Wine Club Members receive 20% off first two tickets purchased._

6:30 p.m.

# **VERITAS SUPPER SERIES**

[****VERITAS SUPPER SERIES****](https://veritaswines.com/supper-series)

# MAY 29TH

# FRIDAY

[**TICKETS ON SALE**](https://www.exploretock.com/veritaswines/event/599815/french-bistro-supper-series-at-veritas)

[**VIEW MENU**](https://veritaswines.com/may-2026-supper-series-menu)

[**LEARN MORE & PURCHASE TICKETS**](https://veritaswines.com/veritas-illuminated)

# Throughout this series, we are partnering with Chefs from a variety of backgrounds and influences to deliver collaborative culinary experiences, elevating the winery experience. We invite you to enjoy the talents of Chef Jeff Potter. View bio. Dine on a six course chef’s tasting menu showcasing unique flavor combinations and inspirations. Wines from the Veritas library will be paired with Chef Potter’s dishes to deliver a complete epicurean journey.

# 6:30 pm

# **SUPPER SERIES ft. CHEF JEFF POTTER**

# MARCH 24TH

# FRIDAY

# **Price:** $225, including wine pairings. _Wine Club Members receive 20% off first two tickets purchased._

Chef Andy was born in Virginia and raised in the Shenandoah Valley, where he lives with his wife and three sons. While studying at the University of Mary Washington in Fredericksburg, he worked for Top Chef contestant Joy Crump at her restaurant FOODE. In 2010, he first joined Veritas as Sous Chef. Three years later, he went down the road and took up the mantle of Sous Chef at the Farmhouse at Veritas. He served as the Chef at the Farmhouse from 2014-2020. When he isn't busy in the kitchen, he enjoys spending time with his family, books, and open-wheel racing.

### **ANDY SHIPMAN**

# Summer at Veritas: Ripening Vines and Remarkable Moments

## August 28, 2025

Summer time, it’s hot and humid, it is the hottest and the most humid month of the year. It’s as if we are dogged by the “Dog Star” Sirius which is the brightest star in the heavens from late July to early August, the so-called “dog days of summer.” Dogged because it is that very heat and humidity makes wine grape- growing in Virginia such a challenge. Part of the reason we created Starry Nights was  to counteract the summer time blues and the dog days of summer.

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/1-Summer-Veritas-1024x718.png)Summer at Veritas

For me August is a peculiar month, it’s a sort of nothing month. You can’t get anything done in August because it seems that everyone is out on vacation. Nowhere is more evident than in France when it seems the whole of Parisian restaurants are “en vacances.”   Nothing is happening in the tasting room, August is typically one of our slowest months when it comes to wine sales and visitation. And nothing is happening in the vineyard,  the nets are up, the canopy is in shape, we simply have to wait for the berries to ripen.

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/3-Netted-Vines-ready-to-pickr-1024x611.png)Netted Vines on Ripe Vioognier

## The Wine is made in the Vineyard

The quality of the wine is directly related to the quality of the grapes we grow so bear with me as we consider the importance of weather conditions to grape growing also known as viticulture. One of the ways farmers and wine-grape growers monitor the amount of heat we are experiencing is a measure called a “Growing Degree Day” or GDD. GDDs vary from plant to plant and it so happens that vines require at least 50 degrees Fahrenheit to grow that’s why wine grape growing is restricted to certain temperature defined areas in the worldWine growing regions across the world

To calculate a growing degree day is very easy, you just add the average daily temperature -highest temperature + the lowest temperature divided by 2 – say 60 +80 -140/2 = 70 and subtract the minimum temperature – 50 = 20 GDD. The growing season is considered to be April, when the buds burst, to the end of October when harvest is over.  GDDs help us predict things like harvest dates as well as knowing the life cycles of different insects that pose a threat to the vines.

As far as this year is concerned we are well above average having a cumulative total of 3166 GDDs as of August 24th

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/5a-GDDs-this-year-in-Afton.png)![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/5b-Cumulative-GDDS-15-and-30-year-averages.png)

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/6-First-harvest-Chardonnay-for-Sparkling-Wine.jpeg)

Interestingly you can see from the graph we are well above both fifteen and thirty year averages for this time of year giving you a good idea as to how temperatures have changed over the years in our little neck of the woods. You would think that with the above average number of GDDs that we will get an above average year for grape growing but just as in Porgy and Bess- “it ain’t necessarily so.” In 2018 we had significantly more GDDs than 2019 but guess what the 2019 vintage wine quality was much better than 2018.  Makes no sense, it was all due to the fact that in 2018 we had rainfall at every critical point in the life cycle of the vine. It rained during fruit set so we had poor pollination of the vines and it rained through August despite the fact that it was warmer, it was warmer at the wrong times that did not benefit the maturation of the grapes.

As you would expect we have started harvesting the grapes already and as usual we pick Chardonnay early for sparkling wine the lower alcohol in the base wine allows for second fermentation in the bottle. After the Chardonnay we always bring in the Sauvignon Blanc relatively early to capture the bright acidity that characterizes our mouth watering Sauvignon Blanc. Next will be Viognier and later into September the reds and last of all the enigmatic Petit Manseng.

## Wine Sales

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/7-VA-Wine-and-Cider-Sales-1.png)

Business is down as you can see from the above slide from the VA Wine Marketing Board. This trend is not unique to Virginia it is a trend not only throughout the United States it is a trend throughout Europe and the rest of the world, actually Europe has seen the biggest decline. In Virginia the biggest drop was in wine distribution down 14.8% whereas all Virginia wine sales were down  4.95% and Farm Winery sales were down 1.88% – bottom line people are drinking less wine in Virginia but no worse than anywhere else.  And it’s not just wine it is wine, beer, and spirits confirmed in the most recent Gallup poll.

Wine is so much more than alcohol according to Tom Wark in his blog [The Spill](https://www.thespill.net/ "The Spill"), your daily drop of wine news – here are the nine reasons why you should prefer wine above any competition.

> 1\. There’s more of it and there is greater choice
>
> 2\. Wine is more intellectually satisfying.
>
> 3\. Wine is easier to drink
>
> 4\. Wine is the most socially acceptable- weddings, celebrations,
>
> 5\. Wine has greater variety
>
> 6\. Wine is environmentally relevant
>
> 7\. Vineyards are beautiful
>
> 8\. Wine is the best accompaniment to food – by far.
>
> 9\. Wineries are more available.

## Wine for the [Wine Club](https://veritaswines.com/wine-club "Wine Club")

Momentarius Tannat 2023

Our latest wine to join our highly successful Momentarius series is the Momentarius Tannat.

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/8-Tannat-Wine-967x1024.png)

Tannat is a relatively unknown grape that originated in South West France centered on a village called Madiran. The Tannat grape  is characterized by thick skin that makes it resistant to disease and is therefore very suitable to Virginia viticulture. There has been a definite up swing of the plantings in Virginia with a total of 78 acres of planted vines (cf Malbec 28 acres).

Producers in Virginia include Barboursville, Breaux, Blenheim, Horton and Chateau Morrisette

Not the first grape you think of when it comes to red wine and in fact when you pour this wine you might even think it was a black wine which is the name this combination of Tannat and Malbec is given in  Madiran France -”Vin-Noir.”

## Tasting Notes:

The dense, deep ruby color is usually associated with a full bodied, tannic wine which is exactly what this wine is. It smells of black fruit, black cherry, blackberry and damson. In the mouth the wine is extraordinarily smooth with wonderfully integrated assertive tannins that support a core of rich black cherry, plum,licorice, dark chocolate and cigar box flavors.The finish is everlasting and intriguingly complex.

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/Kelsey-1.jpeg)

## Person of the summer – Kelsey Greiff Benson

This is Kelsey’s second harvest with us and boy are we glad to have her as one of our cellar managers.  Kelsey comes to us with a degree in Ecology and Evolutionary Biology from the University of Tennessee. She has a wealth of  wine making experience both in the US and in New Zealand working with hands -on experience both in the vineyard and in the day today running a wine lab and every detailed aspect of winemaking. We are indeed,lucky to have such highly qualified, attractive and hard working individual in our dedicated cellar team.

## Supper Series

Our last supper series with Jean-Paul Bourgeois, the man from New Orleans  and the Veritas kitchen team was an absolute blast – the food was as authentic as authentic gets and not only that the food was absolutely delicious.

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/JP-Recap-1024x1024.jpg)August Supper Series Chef Jean-Paul Bourgeois

Our next [supper series](https://www.exploretock.com/veritaswines/event/538058/supper-series-autumn-olive "supper series") is on September 19th that continues in the same vein as our other star studded chefs in which we are highlighting natural farm fed to table cuisine from Autumn Olive Farms don’t miss out it’s booking up fast.

## Family

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/11-The-whole-family.png)Left to right George, Amelia, Isla, Chloe, Charlotte, Elsie, Emily, Andrew, Patricia, Elliott, Hailey, Lydia, Tralyn, Di and Bill

We had a family photo op recently so instead of using my untrained eye I thought it would be nice to share some professional pictures of the whole family in one place at a time

![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/18-HodsonFamily-120-1024x813.jpeg)![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/12-HodsonFamily-201-1024x1015.jpeg)![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/13-Charlotte-Emily-Lydia.png)![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/14-HodsonFamily-48-943x1024.jpeg)![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/15-HodsonFamily-75-2-908x1024.jpeg)![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/17-HodsonFamily-181-891x1024.jpeg)

Thank you for reading the Veritas Summer Newsletter. Everything seems to be changing and yet everything is the same.   Harvest comes and Harvest goes and yet another vintage is bottled and as sure as autumn comes after the summer we will continue to make the best wine that our vines give us and life will go on.

From all the folks at Veritas have a wonderful Labor Day,

Andrew Hodson

Retired Bottlewasher and Raconteur

For several years in my winter newsletter, I used to bemoan the fact that there was no real winter, but this year made up for all those non-winters combined.

### March 16, 2026

There really is something magical about the sudden transformation from pedestrian green to canary yellow from verdure to alizarin crimson and firetruck red. It is not just the change that is a miracle in and of itself, but the incredible contrasts in colors amplified by the close bosomed friend of the maturing sun.

We’ve been in Virginia for 25 years, and this was undoubtedly the longest prolonged spell of cold weather. I have been bemoaning that in the last few winter newsletters or so, we haven’t had a decently cold winter, but this one has made up for it in spades (or shovels of snow).

# Veritas in the Fall: Harvest to Holidays at the Vineyard

## November 25, 2025

![Dirt road with fall foliage](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/1-Autumn-Colors-1015x1024.jpeg)![Veritas Vineyard covered in Fall colors](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/2-Atumn-Colors-1024x768.jpeg)

**My autumnal soliloquy:**

Autumn is busting out all over, and it’s November.

October was lovely, but the autumn show did not start until the first week of November… and boy, what a show!

![Veritas vines in Fall, turning yellow](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/3-Canary-Yellow-1024x732.jpeg)_Canary Yellow_![A red tree in the fall](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/4-Alizarin-crimson--768x1024.jpeg)_Alizarin Crimson_

There really is something magical about the sudden transformation from pedestrian green to canary yellow, from verdure to alizarin crimson and firetruck red. It is not just the change that is a miracle in and of itself, but the incredible contrasts in colors amplified by the close bosomed friend of the maturing sun. Then of course there are the smells of richness, those mellow hints of forest floor and honey, toffee and caramel that emphasize the bounty of the harvest. And always that twinge of melancholy when the first frosts nip the air; there has been something lost, precisely what we cannot be sure of, was it summer, was it the expectation of the harvest bounty, or is it the sense of impending winter? But then, when we are all glorying in the extravaganza of color, it is gone almost overnight; the leaves blow across the road, and it is all gone.

![An orange tree in the fall](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/5-Extravaganza-of-Color-1024x675.jpeg)

## Harvest 2025

Considering the buildup to harvest, things turned out remarkably well. Fruit set in May was marred by cloudy skies. Rainfall in June and July was above average, but in August the sun came out, and all was forgiven. This year, we finished by October 2.

[![Seven Veritas harvest and cellar crew members](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/6-Cellar-Crew.jpeg)](https://veritaswines.com/about)

We were ravaged by predation — by which I mean deer, especially on the top meadow. We’ve always tried to avoid fencing the whole vineyard; we’ve even used dogs to keep the deer out, but I have to admit the dogs could’ve done a better job. It is probably time for us to put up fences on the top meadow.

_Our fabulous, hard-working, stalwart, harvest crew from left to right: Kelsey, Kovie, Chris, Jolie, Elliott, Emily, and Andrew._

### Spotted Lantern Fly

Then, of course, there is the dreaded Spotted Lantern Fly (Lycoderma delicatula) or SLF, the latest pestilence for us to contend with. I mentioned this bad boy in the newsletter a year ago when we had spotted a few (pun intended), but no real reports of damage.

![A graphic depicting the life cycle of the spotted lantern flies](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Screenshot-2025-11-23-144219-1024x624.png)_Picture of Lantern Fly Life Cycle_

This year, they have made their presence all too clear, and we have had to fight back with what we call spot checks. We have been eliminating groups of both the nymphs and the mature insects as they cluster on the vines. We have been able to keep them at bay, but the real threat will be next year.

The preferred host of the SLF is the tree of heaven (Ailanthus altissima). Still, it feeds on other trees and crops, including soybeans, grapes, and stone fruits such as peaches and apricots. The flies feed by biting into the plant’s sap, and as they feed, they excrete a sugary liquid that promotes the growth of black, sooty mildew. Believe it or not, it was first reported in Pennsylvania way back in 2014. We have adopted two main lines of defence, the first to eliminate as many trees of heaven as we can and the second to destroy the eggs that the SLF lays.

![A trunk of a tree covered in adult spotted lantern flies](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/7a-Real-Lif-Spotted-Lantern-Flies-rotated.jpeg)

## Wine of the Season

I like to feature one of our wines with every newsletter, and at the point of sounding like a broken record, I’m featuring our regular [2024 Cabernet Franc](https://shop.veritaswines.com/product/cabernet-franc-2024 "") — last quarter I raved about the [2023 Cabernet Franc Reserve](https://shop.veritaswines.com/product/cabernet-franc-reserve-2023 ""), so this month I’m raving about our latest release.

[![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/SS_VeritasVineyards_October9.2025_10-683x1024.jpg)](https://shop.veritaswines.com/wines/red-wines/)

**Andrew’s Tasting Note:** Medium ruby in color, the 2024 Cabernet Franc has that elusive aroma that is so characteristic yet so difficult to describe. It is a combination of flowers, like violet petals and lilacs, combined with herbs of Provence that intertwine with red fruits, raspberry, red cherry, and blackberry.

With the ever-elusive black pepper and spice notes, the wine is medium-bodied on the palate, with bright fruit around a core of finely textured tannins, leaving a finish with hints of earthiness and a whiff of black pepper. Cabernet Franc pairs with delicate meats like duck and spring lamb as well as salmon and savoury dishes, and anything with a red sauce.

_Photo by Ray Photography Co. taken at our [Secret Supper](https://www.secretsupper.co/supper-series-schedule?srsltid=AfmBOoo1oGrDm2zRvCQPe0y_IJKzjnHZl_hQPJMfj-iVkYkBq3_3lPKe "") dinner on October 9, 2025._

## Andrew’s Wine Line

Not that I’m one for self-promotion, but it is worth noting that, starting on the last Thursday of each month, I have been hosting monthly wine tastings for around 30-35 [wine club members](https://veritaswines.com/wine-club "").  We began in July with [Cabernet Franc](https://shop.veritaswines.com/product/cabernet-franc-2024 ""), followed in August with [Viognier](https://shop.veritaswines.com/product/viognier-2024 ""), in September with [Claret](https://shop.veritaswines.com/product/claret-2023 ""), and in October with [Petit Verdot](https://shop.veritaswines.com/product/petit-verdot-2022 ""). _(We’ll pick these back up again in the new year, in case you are interested in joining us.)_

[![](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/IMG_3138-768x1024.jpg)](https://veritaswines.com/events) _October’s Petit Verdot Wine Line with Andrew Hodson. Photo by Patricia Hodson._

I usually do a brief educational piece about the featured grape. On occasion, [Bill Tonkins](https://veritaswines.com/about ""), our vineyard manager, has shared his knowledge of the grape’s interesting viticultural aspects. The real emphasis, though, is on the tasting of the wines, in particular on the aging effects on each varietal. To make it fun, we have, on a couple of occasions, tasted the wines “blind,” that is, no one knows which wine is in their glass. We taste six wines, four of which are Veritas wines from different vintages, from youngest to oldest, which people call a “vertical tasting.”

I usually throw in a couple of ringers of the same variety from a different country of comparable vintages. At the end of the tasting, I asked the group to vote for which wine each person considered their favorite. To my surprise, with the [red wines](https://shop.veritaswines.com/wines/red-wines/ ""), Cabernet Franc, Claret (not tasted blind), and Petit Verdot, the majority of the group chose the older wines over the younger ones.

Proving in real life with our own wine club members what we have known all along: aging wines improves everything about the wines, but particularly the complexity of the wine.

## Wedding Season at Veritas

[![A Veritas employee headshot](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/JesseeMcDowell-683x1024.jpg)](https://veritaswines.com/about) _Jessee McDowell, Veritas Events Manager and Director of Operations. Wedding season is winding down. We have had a number of weddings on the property this year, and I want to give a special shout-out to Jessee McDowell, who has done a fantastic job leading our events staff. He has ensured that every couple has the best day of their lives!

The [New Year’s Eve Masked Ball](https://www.exploretock.com/veritaswines/event/560925/new-years-eve-masked-ball-2025 "") is booking up fast — and in reality, folks, this is the only show in Afton when it comes to really celebrating New Year’s in fashion. Patrica and I will be in attendance as always, and hope to see you there!

## Employee of the Season

Cody McGehee has been with us on and off since 2021 and is now the Executive Chef at [The Farmhouse at Veritas](https://www.veritasfarmhouse.com/ ""). There’s nowhere between the Farmhouse and the Winery that he hasn’t worked. Cody is a native Virginian and, by any standard, is a self-made man. He started at 15, helping in his family’s business, where he found his calling as a chef. In his early days, he worked in various restaurants in the Lynchburg area. Working alongside Andy Shipman, Cody has proved himself an outstanding chef, wowing the guests at Farmhouse. He is a team player and an invaluable member of Veritas’ culinary team.

[![A Veritas employee headshot](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/SeraPetrasPhotography_VeritasHeadshots2024-6-1-683x1024.jpg)](https://veritaswines.com/about)

_Photo by Sera Petras Photography._

## Family Updates

Patricia and I celebrated our 53rd wedding anniversary on September 30th in San Sebastian, Spain.

![A couple posing with two glasses of wine under umbrellas](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/10-a-Andrew-and-Patricawedding-anniversary-973x1024.jpeg)

## Farewell to Autumn and Thankful Tidings

As the winds strip the leaves from the trees, we prepare for the long, dark days of winter.

![A photo of a bare tree in fall with one leaf remaining on it's branches.](https://veritaswines.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/15-Last-leaf-on-the-tree-875x1024.jpeg)

The beauty is now almost gone, but we are consoled by the prospects of celebrating Thanksgiving within the bosom of friendship and family. As the seasons change, so must we; it is not the strong who survive, but the ones who can adapt.

With all our best wishes for a Happy Thanksgiving and holiday season! See you in the new year, cheers!

Andrew and the entire Veritas Family.
